ARIE 1920-1921 [vol. 043]


A.--List of copper plates examined during the year 1920-21.


ARIE/1920-1921/A/1920-21/1 (page 15)
Placement
The Agent and Diwan to the Hon'ble the Raja of Parlakimedi, Ganjām dis-trict.
Dynasty
Eastern Gaṅga.
King
Mahārāja Dēvēndravarman, son of Guṇārṇava.
Date
184th year of reign.
Language
Sanskrit (in Telugu)
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
Epigraphica Indica.
Remarks
Records the tax-free grant of the village Huḍuvaka in the Pushyagiri-Pañchāli-vishaya, by the king, to his guru Pataṅga-Śivāchārya for guru-pūjā. The latter gave half of the village to (the god) Yōgēśvara-Bhaṭāra.
ARIE/1920-1921/A/1920-21/2 (page 15)
Placement
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Mahārāja Anantavarman, son of Mahārājādhirāja Dēvēn-dravarman.
Date
204th year of reign, Mārga-śīrsha, śukla, trayōdaśī.
Language
Sanskrit (in Telugu)
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
Epigraphica Indica.
Remarks
States that the king made a tax-free gift of the village Tālatthere in Krōshṭuka-varttanī to the venerable scholar Vishṇu-Sōmāchārya of the Parāśara-gōtra residing at Śriṅgāṭika-agrahāra in the Kāmarūpa-vishaya. The grant was made on the occasion of a marriage at the request of the king's brother Jaya-varman.
ARIE/1920-1921/A/1920-21/3 (page 15)
Placement
M.R.Ry. T.C.Rath, B.A., Dis-trict Munsif, Chodavaram, Godavari district.
Dynasty
Śailōdbhava.
King
Dharmarāja
Date
Samva[t] [8]--100 (i.e., 800), Vaiśākha, śu. daśao.
Language
Sanskrit (in Nāgarī)
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
Epigraphica Indica.
Remarks
Records the tax-free gift of half of the village Koṇḍoḍḍa in the Khiḍḍiṅgahāra-vishaya to the Agnihōtri and Bhaṭṭa Gōṇadēvasvāmi of the Kauśika-gōtra and Vājasanēya-charaṇa.
ARIE/1920-1921/A/1920-21/4 (page 15)
Placement
M.R.Ry. Pottam Venkappa Garu of Konakondla through the Tahsildar of Gooty taluk, Anantapur district.
Dynasty
Vijaya-nagara.
King
Kṛishṇarāya
Date
Śaka 1435, Aṅgirasa, Āshāḍha, Śukla-dvādaśī.
Language
Sanskrit (in Nāgarī)
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Registers the grant by the king of the villages Kṛishṇipāḍu, ‘Pinna-Pūsalapāḍu, Pedda-Pūsalapāḍu, Śikēsala and Vēmulapāḍu with the village Daṇḍanāyaka-cheruvu surnamed Kṛishṇarāyasamudram, to a large number of Brahmans on the occasion of the gift of Dhānya-Mēru (i.e., Mēru of grain) The village belonged to the ‘Eḍapti’-sīma of the Gutti-rājya.
ARIE/1920-1921/A/1920-21/5 (page 15)
Placement
M.R.Ry. Busi Nagi Reddi Garu, Vajra-Karur in the same taluk.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Vīrapratāpa Bukkarāya
Date
Śaka 1109, Jaya (wrong), Āśvija, śu. 10.
Language
Telugu
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
A clear forgery. Presumes to register the sever-ahāyagāras (incumbents) like reḍḍi, karaṇam, purōhita, etc., for the villages of Poṭṭipāḍu and Kavuḷūru in the Gutti-durga founded by some private individuals. Reference is made to a certain Sambhaṭi Tipparāju.
ARIE/1920-1921/A/1920-21/6 (page 15)
Placement
M.R.Ry. Chinnappa Reddi of Chittur in the same taluk.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Vīrapratāpa Hariharadēva-Mahārāya, ‘ruling at Vidyānagara’.
Date
Śaka 1093, Vijaya, Vaiśākha ba. 7.
Language
Telugu
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Characters are too late for the date given. Also a forgery. Gives the lands assigned to the several services attached to the village Tarimela in the Gutti-rājya. Lands attached to the local temples of Chenna-kēśvara and Īśvara are also mentioned.
ARIE/1920-1921/A/1920-21/7 (page 15)
Placement
M.R.Ry. Garudacharlu, Dharmakarta, Āñjanēya-svāmin temple at Kasapuram in the same taluk.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Vīrapratāpa Sadāśivarāya-Mahārāya, ‘ruling at Vidyānagara’.
Date
Śaka 1377, mistake for 1477, Rā-kshasa, Śrāvaṇa śu. 5.
Language
Telugu & Sanskrit
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Purports to be an agrahāra-śāsana (gift-deed) granted by the king in respect of the village Neṭekallu, while camping near it on his way to Gutti, being told that god Haṇumān was manifest (jāgrata) there.
ARIE/1920-1921/A/1920-21/8 (page 16)
Placement
M.R.Ry Hanuma Reddi Garu of Konganapalli in the same taluk.
Dynasty
Vijayanagara.
King
Vīrapratāpa Vijaya-Bukkarāya
Date
Śaka 1109, Jaya-(wrong), Āśvija, śu. 10
Language
Telugu
Origin
Returned
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Like No. 5 above is a forgery of the same date giving the several āyagāras for the three villages Koṅganapalle, Śankarabaṇḍa and Mulukalapeṇṭa, which were founded by certain private individuals and mentions the same chief Sambhaṭi Tipparāju.
ARIE/1920-1921/A/1920-21/9 (page 16)
Placement
M.R.Ry. Yella Reddi Garu, Khadarpeta in the same taluk.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Vīrapratāpa Hari-haradēva-Mahārā-ya, ‘ruling at Vid-yānagara.’
Date
Śaka 1270, Sarvajit Vaiśākha, śu. 15.
Language
Telugu & Sanskrit
Origin
Returned
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Registers the grant, of the post of reḍḍi with lands attach-ed to it, to a certain Kōṭireḍḍi Nārapareḍḍi in respect of the village Dēvarapalle in the Gutti-rājya known as Bhāskara-kshētra (i.e., seat of the Sun).
ARIE/1920-1921/A/1920-21/10 (page 16)
Placement
The Reddi of Gundala in the same taluk.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
…
Language
Telugu
Origin
Returned
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Incomplete. Narrates in detail the troubles undergone by a Nāyaka who owned the village Pātakotta-cheruvu in the matter of making good the loss of merchandise sustained by certain merchants while in transit, in the vicinity of the village. The incident is referred to the time of the occupation of the Karṇāṭaka and the Gutti fort by the Nawab of Gōlkoṇḍa on behalf of the Pāchchhāyi (i.e., the Mughal Emperor of Delhi). At its commencement the record quotes the date Śaka 1344, Vijaya (wrong), Kārtika, śu. 10 and refers to the Vijayanagara king Prauḍhadēvarāya.
ARIE/1920-1921/A/1920-21/11 (page 16)
Placement
M.R.Ry. P.Narasimha Reddi Garu of Havili in the same taluk.
Dynasty
Vijayanagara.
King
Sadāśiva-Mahārāya.
Date
Śaka 1481, Siddhā-rthi, Bhādrapaḍā kṛishṇa.
Language
Sanskrit (in Nāgarī)
Origin
Returned
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Incomplete, Plates 2 and 4 are missing. Registers the sarvamānya grant of some double-crop (dvisāra) land in the village Chembāla lying in the Rāyadurga-veṇṭe (i.e., province) and Uruvakoṇḍa-śīma for the benefit of the tem-ple of Chennakēśvara built on the east side of the village.
ARIE/1920-1921/A/1920-21/12 (page 16)
Placement
The District Munsif of Kavali, Nellore district.
Dynasty
Gajapati
King
Pratāparudra
Date
Śaka 1432, Pramō-da, Kārtika, śu. 3, Friday.
Language
Sanskrit (in Telugu)
Origin
Returned
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Registers the grant of the village Velicherla in the Jala-daṅki-sthala of the Pāṅkanāṭi-sīma to the east of the Udayāchala (i.e., Udayagiri)-durga, by the king who was ruling at Uṇḍrakoṇḍa, to the Brahman Koṇḍaya of the Bhāradvāja-gōtra and Yajuś-śākhā. The donee was a resident of the village Puluguḷḷa.
ARIE/1920-1921/A/1920-21/13 (page 16)
Placement
M.R.Ry. Perumal Gowndan, Gudi-yattam taluk, North Arcot dis-trict.
Dynasty
…
King
Ālavagiri Bāshā (Ālamgir ?).
Date
Śaka 1012 (wrong), Krōdhana. Vaiyā-śi, 21, ba., pañ-chamī, Monday, Śravaṇa.
Language
Tamil
Origin
Returned
Edition
…
Remarks
States that a family of seven gauṇḍas, which hailed from Vēlūr-śīrmai on the northern bank of the Pālār river in Āyinḍa-nāḍu, a sub-division of Paḷuvūr-kōṭṭam, a dis-trict of Jayaṅgoṇḍa-Toṇḍamaṇḍalam and which settled down near Vēlūr having founded the village of Lattēri by clearing the forest, succeeded in repulsing the attack of a band of 500 freebooters who came from the north and that as a reward for this act of heroism Abarangbeg-Pāshā conferred on the gauṇḍas the headmanship (?) (gauḍikai) of the village of Lattēri with right to collect one kalam of grain on every kāṇi of certain lands specified therein. The record seems to be a forgery.
ARIE/1920-1921/A/1920-21/14 (page 17)
Placement
M.R.Ry Rao Bahadur V.A. Van-dayar Avargal, Managing Mem-ber, Temple Committee, Tanjore.
Dynasty
Mahrattas of Tanjore.
King
Praṭāpasiṁha
Date
Śaka 1680, Kali 4862, Pramādi, Tai 21, Uttarāya-ṇa, Thursday, Pushya.
Language
Tamil
Origin
Returned
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Registers that Savāyī Vijayaraghunātha Gōpālar, son of Savāyi Vijayaraghunātha Kiṇamettanan Gōpālar, who was the chief of Sirunellikkōṭṭai in Pāmba-vaḷanāḍu, a sub-division of Rājeṅdraśōḻa-vaḷanāḍu in Rājagaṁbhīra-vaḷanāḍu, a district of Rājarāja-vaḷanāḍu, gave 46 poṉ of gold to the temple Jayaṅgoṇḍanāthasvāmin in Pāmba-nāḍu for the evening service of the god therein. Another record dated in Śaka 1690, Kali 4860, Īśvara, Vaigāśi, 2, is engraved in continuation of the above on the same plate and registers a gift of 45 Rājagōpālaṉchakram-poṉ of gold by the inhabitants of the sixteen divisions between the western and eastern boundaries of Pāppākkuḍi-nāḍu, a sub-division of Poyyūr-kūṟṟam, a district of Jayaṅgoṇḍa-nāḍu, for the midday service of the god Jayaṅgoṇḍanātha-svāmin consecrated in a temple which was newly erected after clearing some fruit-gardens.
ARIE/1920-1921/A/1920-21/15 (page 17)
Placement
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Do.
Date
Śaka 1680, Kali, 4861, Bahudhān-ya, Āṉi. 16, Uttarāyaṇa, Monday.
Language
Tamil
Origin
Returned
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Records a further gift of 91 poṉ and 2 paṇam by the individual mentioned in No. 14 above for conducting a service called Kōlāhala-śandi in the same temple. The poṉ (gold coin) is called Rājagōpālachakram. Another record in continuation of the above registers the gift of 46 Rājagōpālaṉchakram-poṉ by Rāmaviruda Vijayā-dēvar, son of Umayānallavaṉ Vijayādēvar of Neṉmali-vāḍi in Śirunellikōṭṭai, a portion of Pāppākkuḍi-nāḍu, a sub-division Poyyūr-kūṟṟam, a district of Rājarāja-vaḷa-nāḍu, Rājēndraśōḻa-vaḷanāḍu for the midnight offerings to the god mentioned in No. 14 above. This supplemental record is dated in Kali 1680, Śaka 4861 (transposed), Bahu-dhānya, Vaigāśi 2.
ARIE/1920-1921/A/1920-21/16 (page 17)

M.R.Ry. K.V.Lakshmana Rao Garu, M.A., Diwan of Muna-gala.

Bāḍapa

…

Records the grant of the village Ārumbāka in the Velanāṇḍu-vishaya by the king to the chief Gaṇḍanārāyaṇa and its grant by the latter to his mother's sister's son Chandena; see below Part II, paragraph 14.

ARIE/1920-1921/B/1920/326 (page 18)
Placement
On a stone built into the western wall of the mosque near the cemetery in the same village.
Dynasty
Vijayanagara
King
Harihara
Date
Lost
Language
Sanskrit (verse)
Remarks
Damaged. Gives in succession a list of Jaina teachers of the Koṇḍakunda line, viz., Vakragrīva, E1lāchārya, Amarakīrti, Siṁhanandi, and Vardhamāna-Dēśika and refers to the building of a Chaityālaya (Jaina basti) for Pārśva-Jinanātha by the general Iruga. The country Kuntala is herein said to be a part of Karṇāṭa.

GUNTUR DISTRICT,


TENALI TALUK.


ARIE/1920-1921/B/1920/628 (page 44)
Placement
On a rough stone set up in a street at Amritalur.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Pramōda, Jyēsṭha, ba., 13, Wednes-day.
Language
Telugu
Remarks
Registers the agreement (Kaulu) granted by Mahāmaṇḍalēś-vara Chintaguṇṭa Timmarājayya to the people that settled at the pēṭa (market village) built by him to the south of Amritalūru in the name of Mahānandirāja. No taxes were payable by the settlers in the pēṭa for the first three years. After that period they were required to pay taxes on ploughs, looms, and houses, big and small.

ARIE/1920-1921/B/1920/659 (page 47)
Placement
On the southern side of the eastern gateway of the same temple.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
…
Language
Sanskrit & Telugu
Remarks
Defines in a ślōka the lengṭhs of the linear measures of aṅguḷa, vitasti and daṇḍaka. Half of the circum-ference of the thumb is an aṅguḷa. Twelve aṅguḷas make one vitasti and thirty-two vitastis make one daṇḍaka. In the Telugu portion the kēsaripāṭi-ghaḍa which corres-ponds to the daṇḍaka is mentioned. A vertical line is cut over the inscription to give the exact measurement, evi-dently, of the vitasti. It measures a little over 1 foot and 3 inches.

Language
Telugu verse & prose
Remarks
Registers the grant of 50 sheep for a perpetual lamp in the temple of Toṇḍīśvara at Īvani by Kāmaka of Ghaṇṭaśāla for the merit of her father Pōtināyaka and her mother Prōlama and the grant of a house-site and land by her to the custodian of the sheep who was to supply daily the ghee for the said lamp.

ARIE/1920-1921/B/1920/695 (page 51)
Placement
On a pillar built into the wall of the Rājēśvara temple at Peda-konduru.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1092
Language
Sanskrit verse & Telugu
Remarks
Records a gift of land and cows made for two perpetual lamps to the god Rājarjāēśvara by the Śiva-Brāhmaṇa Mallidēva of Koṇḍrūru. In the introduction is described the family of the chief [Ka]nda, who was the ‘lord of Koṇḍrūru’ and who served under King Vikrama-Chōḍadēva. Kanda's sons were Kāma, Drōṇa Bhīma and Rāma.
ARIE/1920-1921/B/1920/696 (page 51)
Placement
On the same pillar
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1095
Language
Sanskrit verse & Telugu
Remarks
States that Rāma, the son of the chief Kanda (mentioned in the above record) who was also the ‘lord of Koṇḍrūru’ and who was much devoted to the Śivadharma gave land for the offerings and perpetual lamp of the god Rājarājē-śvara. In the Telugu portion are given the names of the dancing girls who were attached to the temple of Rāja-rājēśvara.

Tamil
